## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the fundamental problem of population dynamics. The growth rate typically depends on current population through density-dependent feedback mechanisms, and may include explicit time dependence for seasonal or environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * P * (1 - c1 * P) (cooperative growth at low density)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoidal growth model)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent birth minus death)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (growth with constant removal rate)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal variation in growth)
- Exponential decay approach: dP_dt = c0 * (c1 - P) (linear approach to carrying capacity)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (cubic density response)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P (dP_dt proportional to P) → exponential/Malthusian regime indicating density-independent growth
- Quadratic term in P (P² with negative coefficient) → density-dependent self-limitation, characteristic of logistic-type carrying capacity
- Cubic terms in P (positive P² and negative P³) → Allee effect where growth is reduced at both low and high densities
- Logarithmic coupling log(P) multiplied by P → Gompertz-type asymmetric growth where decline rate accelerates near carrying capacity
- Ratio of polynomials in P → Holling-type functional responses or Beverton-Holt recruitment dynamics
- Product of multiple linear factors in P → multiple equilibria / critical population thresholds in the dynamics
- Sinusoidal dependence on t multiplied by growth terms → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on reproduction
- Growth rate vanishing at P=0 (no constant term) → biological consistency requiring zero growth with no individuals present
- Fractional powers of P (P^(2/3) or P^(3/4)) → metabolic scaling laws relating body/colony size to growth rate
- Exponential dependence on t in coefficients → environmental degradation or improvement affecting carrying capacity over time

**GT expression:**
```
0.201*(-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233)*P + 0.201*P + 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(-0.634 + P)))
```

Let me expand this:

**First term:** 0.201*(-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233)*P

Let me expand (-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233):
= -1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P²/(5.637*10.233)
= -1 + P*(1/10.233 + 1/5.637) - P²/57.683

So the first term = 0.201*P*[-1 + P*(0.0977 + 0.1774) - P²*0.01734]
= 0.201*(-P + 0.2751*P² - 0.01734*P³)
= -0.201*P + 0.05530*P² - 0.003486*P³

**Second term:** 0.201*P

**Third term:** 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(P - 0.634)))

Combining first and second terms:
- P terms: -0.201*P + 0.201*P = 0
- P² term: 0.05530*P²
- P³ term: -0.003486*P³

**So GT = -0.003486*P³ + 0.05530*P² + 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(P - 0.634)))**

Now, the sigmoid function: P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-b))) relates to tanh via:
1/(1 + exp(-x)) = (1 + tanh(x/2))/2

So: 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(P - 0.634))) = 0.201*P * (1 + tanh(5.637*(P-0.634)/2))/2
= 0.1005*P + 0.1005*P*tanh(2.8185*P - 1.787)

**So GT = -0.003486*P³ + 0.05530*P² + 0.1005*P + 0.1005*P*tanh(2.8185*P - 1.787)**

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.201*(-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233)*P + 0.201*P + 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(-0.634 + P)))
```

Let me expand this:
- First term: `0.201*(-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233)*P` — this is a cubic polynomial in P
- Second term: `0.201*P` — linear in P
- Third term: `0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(-0.634 + P)))` — this is `c*P*sigmoid(a*(P-b))`

The sigmoid function `1/(1 + exp(-x))` can be written as `(1 + tanh(x/2))/2`.

So the third term: `0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(P - 0.634)))` = `0.201*P * sigmoid(5.637*(P-0.634))`

Using `sigmoid(x) = (1 + tanh(x/2))/2`:
= `0.201*P * (1 + tanh(5.637*(P-0.634)/2))/2`
= `0.201*P/2 + 0.201*P*tanh(2.819*(P-0.634))/2`
= `0.1005*P + 0.1005*P*tanh(2.819*P - 1.787)`

So the full GT becomes:
- Cubic in P (from first term): `0.201*P*(-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233)` which expands to `aP³ + bP² + cP`
- Plus `0.201*P`
- Plus `0.1005*P + 0.1005*P*tanh(2.819*P - 1.787)`

Combining: **GT = αP³ + βP² + γP + δP·tanh(εP + ζ)**

where all constants are specific numbers. This is exactly the form:
`P³*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2*tanh(P*c3 + c4) + P*c5`

The GT has **no dependence on t**, and the functional form is: cubic polynomial in P plus P*tanh(linear in P).
